interface for sending a batch of samples to an\n404: // external timeseries database.\n405: type WriteClient interface {\n406: \t// Store stores the given samples in the remote storage.\n407: read or write endpoint for the storage client.\n411: \tEndpoint() string\n412: }\n413: \n414: // QueueManager manages a queue of samples to be sent to the Storage\n415: // indicated by the provided            client,\n504: \t\tsendExemplars:           enableExemplarRemoteWrite,\n505: \t\tsendNativeHistograms:    enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite,\n506: \t\tenableTypeAndUnitLabels: \n522: \t\tmetrics:  metrics,\n523: \t\tinterner: interner,\n524: \n525: \t\tprotoMsg: protoMsg,\n526: \t\tcompr:    compression.Snappy, // Hardcoded for now, but scaffolding exists for likely future use.\n527: \t}\n528: \n529: \twalMetadata := t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1\n530: \n531: \tt.watcher = wlog.NewWatcher(watcherMetrics, readerMetrics, logger, client.Name(), t, dir, enableExemplarRemoteWrite, enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite, walMetadata)\n532: \n533: \t// The current MetadataWatcher implementation is mutually exclusive\n534: \t// with the new approach, which stores metadata as WAL records and\n535: \t// ships them alongside series. If both mechanisms are set, the new one\n536: \t// takes precedence by implicitly disabling the older one.\n537: \tif t.mcfg.Send && t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n538: \t\tlogger.Warn(\"usage of 'metadata_config.send' is redundant when using remote write v2 (or higher) as metadata will always be gathered from the WAL and included for every series within each write request\")\n539: \t\tt.mcfg.Send = false\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n543: \t\tt.metadataWatcher = NewMetadataWatcher(logger, sm, client.Name(), t, t.mcfg.SendInterval, flushDeadline)\n544: \t}\n545: \tt.shards = t.newShards()\n546: \n547: \treturn t\n548: }\n549: \n550: // AppendWatcherMetadata sends metadata to the remote storage. Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := t.sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx, mm[i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend:last], pBuf)\n574: \t\tif err != nil {\n575: \t\t\tt.metrics.failedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(last - (i * t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n576: \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := func(try int) error {\n591: \t\tctx, span := otel.Tracer(\"\").Start(ctx, \"Remote Metadata Send Batch\")\n592: \t\tdefer span.End()\n593: \n594: \t\tspan.SetAttributes(\n595: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"metadata\", metadataCount),\n596: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"try\", try),\n597: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_name\", t.storeClient.Name()),\n598: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_url\", t.storeClient.Endpoint()),\n599: \t\t)\n600: \t\t// Attributes defined by OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n601: \t\tif try > 0 {\n602: \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n603: \t\t}\n604: \n605: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n606: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since it's\n607: \t\t// embedded in v2 calls now, and we do v1 here.\n608: \t\t_, err := t.storeClient.Store(ctx, req, try)\n609: \t\tt.metrics.sentBatchDuration.Observe(time.Since(begin).Seconds())\n610: \n611: \t\tif err != nil {\n612: \t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n613: \t\t\treturn err\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\treturn nil\n616: \t}\n617: \n618: \tretry := func() {\n619: \t\tt.metrics.retriedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n620: \t}\n621: \terr = t.sendWriteRequestWithBackoff(ctx, attemptStore, retry)\n622: \tif err != nil {\n623: \t\treturn err\n624: \t}\n625: \tt.metrics.metadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n626: \tt.metrics.metadataBytesTotal.Add(float64(len(req)))\n627: \treturn nil\n628: }\n629: \n630: func isSampleOld(baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration, ts int64) bool {\n631: \tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n632: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n633: \t\treturn false\n634: \t}\n635: \tlimitTs := baseTime.Add(-sampleAgeLimit)\n636: \tsampleTs := timestamp.Time(ts)\n637: \treturn sampleTs.Before(limitTs)\n638: }\n639: \n640: func isTimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n641: \treturn func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n642: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n643: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n644: \t\t\treturn false\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tswitch {\n647: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n648: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n649: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n650: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n651: \t\t\t\treturn true\n652: \t\t\t}\n653: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n654: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Histograms[0].Timestamp) {\n655: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n656: \t\t\t\treturn true\n657: \t\t\t}\n658: \t\tcase len(ts.Exemplars) > 0:\n659: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Exemplars[0].Timestamp) {\n660: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n661: \t\t\t\treturn true\n662: \t\t\t}\n663: \t\tdefault:\n664: \t\t\treturn false\n665: \t\t}\n666: \t\treturn false\n667: \t}\n668: }\n669: \n670: func isV2TimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n671: \treturn func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n672: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n673: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n674: \t\t\treturn false\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t\tswitch {\n677: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n678: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n679: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n680: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n681: \t\t\t\treturn true\n682: \t\t\t}\n683: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n684: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Histograms[0].Timestamp) {\n685: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n686: \t\t\t\treturn true\n687: \t\t\t}\n688: \t\tcase len(ts.Exemplars) > 0:\n689: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Exemplars[0].Timestamp) {\n690: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n691: \t\t\t\treturn true\n692: \t\t\t}\n693: \t\tdefault:\n694: \t\t\treturn false\n695: \t\t}\n696: \t\treturn false\n697: \t}\n698: }\n699: \n700: // Append queues a sample to be sent to the remote storage. Blocks until all samples are\n701: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n702: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n703: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n704: outer:\n705: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n706: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n707: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n711: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n712: \t\tif !ok {\n713: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n714: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n715: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n716: \t\t\t} else {\n717: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n718: \t\t\t}\n719: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n720: \t\t\tcontinue\n721: \t\t}\n722: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n723: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n724: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n725: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n726: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. This should not be t.cfg.MinBackoff\n727: \t\t// as it can happen without errors, and we want to pickup work after\n728: \t\t// filling a queue/resharding as quickly as possible.\n729: \t\t// TODO: Consider using the average duration of a request as the backoff.\n730: \t\tbackoff := model.Duration(5 * time.Millisecond)\n731: \t\tfor {\n732: \t\t\tselect {\n733: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n734: \t\t\t\treturn false\n735: \t\t\tdefault:\n736: \t\t\t}\n737: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{\n738: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n739: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n740: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:    s.T,\n741: \t\t\t\tvalue:        s.V,\n742: \t\t\t\tsType:        tSample,\n743: \t\t\t}) {\n744: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n745: \t\t\t}\n746: \n747: \t\t\tt.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n748: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n749: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n750: \t\t\t// It is reasonable to use t.cfg.MaxBackoff here, as if we have hit\n751: \t\t\t// the full backoff we are likely waiting for external resources.\n752: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n753: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n754: \t\t\t}\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t}\n757: \treturn true\n758: }\n759: \n760: func (t *QueueManager) AppendExemplars(exemplars []record.RefExemplar) bool {\n761: \tif !t.sendExemplars {\n762: \t\treturn true\n763: \t}\n764: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n765: outer:\n766: \tfor _, e := range exemplars {\n767: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), e.T) {\n768: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n769: \t\t\tcontinue\n770: \t\t}\n771: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n772: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[e.Ref]\n773: \t\tif !ok {\n774: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[e.Ref]; !ok {\n775: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped exemplar for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", e.Ref)\n776: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n777: \t\t\t} else {\n778: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n779: \t\t\t}\n780: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n781: \t\t\tcontinue\n782: \t\t}\n783: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[e.Ref]\n784: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n785: \t\t// This will only loop if the queues are being resharded.\n786: \t\tbackoff := t.cfg.MinBackoff\n787: \t\tfor {\n788: \t\t\tselect {\n789: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n790: \t\t\t\treturn false\n791: \t\t\tdefault:\n792: \t\t\t}\n793: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(e.Ref, timeSeries{\n794: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels:   lbls,\n795: \t\t\t\tmetadata:       meta,\n796: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:      e.T,\n797: \t\t\t\tvalue:          e.V,\n798: \t\t\t\texemplarLabels: e.Labels,\n799: \t\t\t\tsType:          tExemplar,\n800: \t\t\t}) t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n808: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n809: \t\t\t}\n810: \t\t}\n811: \t}\n812: \treturn true\n813: }\n814: \n815: func (t *QueueManager) AppendHistograms(histograms []record.RefHistogramSample) bool {\n816: \tif !t.sendNativeHistograms {\n817: \t\treturn true\n818: \t}\n819: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n820: outer:\n821: \tfor _, h := range histograms {\n822: that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", h.Ref)\n831: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n832: \t\t\t} else {\n833: \t\t\t\treturn false\n846: \t\t\tdefault:\n847: \t\t\t}\n848: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(h.Ref, timeSeries{\n849: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n850: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n851: \t\t\t\ttimestamp: \treturn true\n867: }\n868: \n869: func (t *QueueManager) AppendFloatHistograms(floatHistograms []record.RefFloatHistogramSample) bool {\n870: \tif !t.sendNativeHistograms {\n871: \t\treturn *QueueManager) Start() {\n926: \t// Register and initialise some metrics.\n927: \tt.metrics.register()\n928: \tt.metrics.shardCapacity.Set(float64(t.cfg.Capacity))\n929: \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n930: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n931: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n932: and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n954: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n955: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n956: \tt.shards.stop()\n957: \tt.watcher.Stop()\n958: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n959: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Stop()\n960: \t}\n961: \tt.metrics.unregister()\n962: }\n963: \n964: // StoreSeries keeps track of which series we know about for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n969: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n970: \tfor _, s := range series {\n971: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert into seriesSegmentIndexes map StoreMetadata(meta []record.RefMetadata) {\n988: \tif t.protoMsg == config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n989: \t\treturn\n990: \t}\n991: \n992: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n993: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n994: \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. Used when only client specific\n1034: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1035: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1036: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1037: \tt.storeClient = c\n1038: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1039: }\n1040: \n1041: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1042: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1043: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1044: \treturn t.storeClient\n1045: }\n1046: \n1047: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. If b contains\n1048: // a label in externalLabels, the value in b wins.\n1049: func processExternalLabels(b *labels.Builder, externalLabels []labels.Label) {\n1050: \tfor _, el := range externalLabels {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1217: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1218: \n1219: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1220: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1221: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown    atomic.Uint32\n1231: \texemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown  atomic.Uint32\n1232: \thistogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown atomic.Uint32\n1233: \tmetadataDroppedOnHardShutdown   atomic.Uint32\n1234: }\n1235: \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = newQueue(s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, s.qm.cfg.Capacity)\n1247: \t}\n1248: \n1249: \ts.queues = newQueues\n1250: \n1251: \tvar hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n1252: \thardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n1265: \t}\n1266: }\n1267: \n1268: // stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.\n1269: func (s *shards) stop() {\n1270: \t// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1329: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()\n1330: \t\t\ts.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()\n1331: \t\tcase tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:\n1332: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()\n1333: \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1334: \t\tdefault:\n1335: \t\t\treturn true\n1336: \t\t}\n1337: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1338: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1361: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1362: \ttimestamp      int64\n1363: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1364: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1365: \tsType seriesType\n1366: }\n1367: \n1368: type seriesType int\n1369: \n1370: const (\n1371: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1372: \ttExemplar\n1373: \ttHistogram\n1374: \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch: being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1446: // made after this is called.\n1447: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1448: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1449: \t\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\n1450: \t}\n1451: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1452: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1453: \tq.batch = nil\n1454: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1455: }\n1456: \n1457: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = func(int) error, onRetry func()) error {\n1982: \tbackoff := t.cfg.MinBackoff\n1983: \tsleepDuration := model.Duration(0)\n1984: \ttry := 0\n1985: \n1986: \tfor {\n1987: \t\tselect {\n1988: \t\tcase duration specified by Retry-After header\", \"duration\", sleepDuration)\n2010: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter < 0:\n2011: \t\t\tt.logger.Debug(\"retry-after cannot be in past, retrying using default backoff mechanism\")\n2012: \t\t}\n2013: \n2014: \t\t// We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015: \t\t// make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016: \t\t//\n2017: \t\t// reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018: \t\t// is disabled. \t\tif value.CompareAndSwap(current, newValue) {\n2061: \t\t\treturn current, true\n2062: \t\t}\n2063: \t}\n2064: }\n2065: \n2066: func buildTimeSeries(timeSeries []prompb.TimeSeries, filter The issue is described as \"after resharding, some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.\"\n\nLet me trace through the flow:\n1. `updateShardsLoop()` decides resharding is needed and sends to `reshardChan` (line 1072)\n2. `reshardLoop()` receives it (line 1189)\n3. It calls `t.shards.stop()` (line 1193)\n4. It calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` (line 1194)\n\nNow, the key insight is in the enqueue function at line 1312-1341:\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n    s.mtx.RLock()\n    defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n    shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))  // <-- THIS LINE IS THE PROBLEM!\n    select {\n    case <-s.softShutdown:\n        return false\n    default:\n        appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n        ...\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe shard number is calculated as: `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))`\n\nNow here's the race condition:\n1. Old shards have N queues, say N=4\n2. Sample arrives for shard 2 (ref % 4 = 2)\n3. At the same time, resharding happens from N=4 to N=6\n4. During stop(): `softShutdown` channel is closed, preventing new enqueues\n5. During start(): new queues are created with N=6\n\nBut here's the problem! Between `stop()` and `start()`, there's a window where:\n\n\n- The old shards are shutting down\n- WAL watcher or Append calls might still try to enqueue data with the OLD shard count\n- When the new shards start, the shard number assignment changes: what was shard 2 out of 4 is now shard 2 out of 6\n\nI need to examine the stop() and start() logic more carefully to understand how samples get lost during this transition.\n\nIn start(), the pending samples counter gets reset to zero, new queues are created for the new shard count, and then s.queues is replaced entirely. Meanwhile, stop() closes the soft shutdown channel and then locks the mutex to clear the queues. The issue is that between when stop() closes softShutdown and when it acquires the lock to clear queues, any Append calls still executing could enqueue samples into the old queues that are about to be discarded. Looking at the enqueue logic more carefully, when `softShutdown` is closed, the function returns false immediately, preventing any new samples from being added. The shard calculation happens before checking the shutdown state, but that's not the actual problem since the check short-circuits the operation.\n\nThe real issue is the timing between when `softShutdown` closes and when the new shards are fully initialized. If a sample arrives after shutdown begins but before the replacement shards are ready, it could be lost or routed incorrectly depending on the exact sequence of lock acquisitions and releases. The problem is that `t.numShards` gets updated in `updateShardsLoop()` immediately after sending the reshard signal, but before the actual resharding completes in `reshardLoop()`. This means new enqueue attempts see the updated shard count while the old shards are still shutting down and new ones haven't started yet. The WAL watcher retries failed enqueues, but they keep failing because the queues are in this transitional state where `numShards` has changed but the actual shard infrastructure hasn't caught When `start()` is called (line 1241), it sets `pendingSamples` to 0\n2. This is correct because the new queues are empty at that point\n3. Actually, let me look at the whole reshardLoop and see if there's a race condition:\n\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n    defer t.wg.Done()    for {\n        select {        case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n            t.shards.stop()        // <-- Stop old shards\n            t.shards.start(numShards)  // <-- Start new shards\n        case <-t.quit:\n            return        }\n    }\n}```\n\nAnd the updateShardsLoop:\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n    ...    for {\n        select {        case <-ticker.C:\n            desiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n            if !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {                continue\n            }\n            select {\n            case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:                t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n                t.numShards = desiredShards  // <-- THIS IS WRONG!\n            default:\n                t.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n            }\n        case <-t.quit:\n            return\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe core issue is at line 1074 where `t.numShards = desiredShards` gets updated immediately. The reshardChan is processed asynchronously by reshardLoop(), so updating the shard count before the actual stop/start sequence completes creates a race condition. The `t.numShards` field should only be updated after reshardLoop() finishes the operation, not when the message is sent. shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n\nSo enqueue() correctly derives the shard index from the actual queue length rather than t.numShards. But I'm noticing something else in the start() method - there's a metrics reset happening that could be problematic. The pendingSamples counter is being set to zero when start() is called, which might not align with the actual state of pending data in the queues.\n\nThe issue is that old shards are still flushing their data asynchronously after stop() is called, and they're decrementing the same pendingSamples counter. By resetting it to zero before those old shards finish their work, the counter loses accuracy about what's actually pending. Even though the old shards are separate objects, they share the same metrics counter with the new shards, so their decrements still affect the global count. call `queue.FlushAndShutdown()` which sends their samples\n4. Each shard, when it finishes sending, calls `updateMetrics()` which decrements `pendingSamples`\n5. At the same time, `start()` is called on a NEW shards object\n6. `start()` sets `pendingSamples.Set(0)`\n7. This resets the counter that the old shards are trying to decrement!\n\nSo the race condition is:\n- Old shards are decrementing `pendingSamples` as they flush\n- New shards are being created and immediately set `pendingSamples` to 0\n- This loses the pending samples counter\n\nLooking more carefully at the reshardLoop, when a reshard happens, the old shards object is replaced with a new one stored back to `t.shards`. However, the old shards continue running in their own goroutines and still reference `s.qm` (the QueueManager). Since both old and new shards share the same `s.qm.metrics` object, there's a race: old shards decrement `pendingSamples` as they finish flushing while new shards immediately reset it to 0, corrupting the counter. The pending samples counter gets reset to zero when resharding begins, but after the new shards are created and their goroutines start running via `runShard()`, samples end up stuck in the queues. When `stop()` closes the old `softShutdown` channel, the new shards don't receive that signal because they're listening on a different channel. The old shards might still be trying to send on closed queues or waiting on a context that never gets cancelled.\n\nLet me trace the shutdown sequence: `stop()` closes the old `softShutdown`, then calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on the old queues. Now I see the issue! Look at line 737:\n\n```go\nif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{...}) {\n    continue outer\n}\n```\n\nThe WAL watcher calls `t.shards.enqueue()` in a loop, retrying with backoff if the enqueue fails. The enqueue() function returns false when:\n1. `softShutdown` is closed (line 1317-1318)\n2. The queue is full (line 1321-1322)\n\nNow, here's the race condition:\n\n1. During resharding, `updateShardsLoop()` sends to `reshardChan` and the `reshardLoop()` processes it\n2. `reshardLoop()` calls `t.shards.stop()` which closes `softShutdown`\n3. This makes `t.shards.enqueue()` return false\n4. The WAL watcher retries the enqueue with backoff (line 748-754)\n5. But during this time, `t.shards.start()` is called, replacing `t.shards` with a new shards object\n6. The new shards object has new empty queues and a new `softShutdown` channel\n\nBut here's the subtle bug! Look at the enqueue() logic again (lines 1312-1341):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n    s.mtx.RLock()\n    defer s.mtx.RUnlock()    shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n    select {\n    case <-s.softShutdown:        return false\n    default:\n        appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n        if !appended {\n            return false        }\n        switch data.sType {\n        case tSample:\n            s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n        ...    }\n}```\n\nAnd the start() method resets the counter:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- RESETS THE COUNTER!\n```\n\nThe race emerges when a sample gets enqueued into the old shards and increments `pendingSamples`, but then `start()` is called on the new shards object and zeroes out the metric before the old sample is actually processed and decremented. The real problem is that `start()` unconditionally resets `pendingSamples` to 0, even when old shards are still draining. If samples from the previous shards haven't finished sending yet, they'll decrement a counter that's already been zeroed out, creating a mismatch between the actual pending count and what the metric reports. The old shards continue running in the background after `stop()` is called, so resetting the counter before they've fully flushed introduces a race condition where the counter no longer reflects reality.\n\nLooking at the actual symptom—metrics showing shards stuck with `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` > 0 but no progress—suggests the new shards are accepting samples but something prevents them from being sent. When `start()` initializes fresh queues and launches new `runShard` goroutines, it's possible the new shards aren't properly connected to the sending mechanism, or there's a synchronization issue that Looking at `runShard()` again:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n    ...\n    batchQueue := queue.Chan()  // <-- Get the channel from the queue\n    ...\n    for {\n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            // Hard shutdown\n            ...\n        case batch, ok := <-batchQueue:\n            if !ok {\n                return  // Queue channel closed\n            }\n            sendBatch(batch, ...)\n        case <-timer.C:\n            // Timeout, flush partial batch\n            batch := queue.Batch()\n            ...\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAnd in `start()`:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    ...\n    var hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n    hardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())  // <-- NEW context!\n    ...\n    for i := range n {\n        go s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n    }\n}\n```\n\nEach time `start()` is called, a NEW context is created. So the new runShard goroutines wait on the NEW context.\n\n\nThe bug emerges in `stop()`: when `s.hardShutdown()` cancels the context, it terminates the current runShard goroutines. But if `start()` gets called again before `stop()` completes, new goroutines spawn with a fresh context—and the old ones never properly clean up because they're already listening to a cancelled context.\n\nThe race unfolds like this: old shards with context C1 and queues Q1-Q4 begin shutting down via `FlushAndShutdown()`, yet the runShard goroutines still exist. Before the old shards fully terminate, new shards initialize with context C2 and different queues Q1'-Q6. The fresh runShard goroutines start consuming from the new queues while the old ones are already dead, leaving the WAL in an inconsistent state where writes might target the wrong shard or queue.\n\nThe core issue is in the enqueue calculation—it uses the current queue count to determine which shard receives data. When resharding from 4 to 6 queues, the modulo operation changes: `ref % 4` produces different results than `ref % 6` for the same reference. This means a series that was routed to queue 2 under the old configuration could be routed to queue 4 under the new one, causing data to land in the wrong place if the old and new shards overlap in time.\n\nThe reshardLoop stops the old shards and replaces `t.shards` with the new object, so subsequent enqueue calls use the updated queue count. However, if samples are still being processed from the old shard configuration while the new one starts, there's a window where routing becomes inconsistent. The real problem emerges in updateShardsLoop when it calculates desired shards and triggers the reshard—there's no guarantee that pending samples from the old configuration are fully drained before the new configuration takes over. pending samples in the old shards are being decremented as they flush, but then `start()` resets the counter to 0, which could cause issues if the old shards haven't finished draining yet. The real problem might be that reshardChan is full—when the select hits the default case, the reshard request gets skipped entirely, potentially leaving the system stuck in a blocked state where resharding never actually completes.\n\nLooking at the actual symptom—some shards showing `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck above zero with no progress—this suggests either samples are queued but not being sent, or the pending count isn't being decremented correctly. The new shards' runShard goroutines might not be starting properly after resharding, which would explain why samples accumulate without being flushed.\n\nIn the start() method, I notice `s.softShutdown` is initialized after the metrics are reset but before the runShard goroutines are spawned. The enqueue() function likely checks this channel, so there's a potential race condition where samples could be enqueued to queues that don't have active consumers yet, or the shutdown signal isn't properly synchronized with the goroutine startup.\n\nLooking at the stop() method, it closes `s.softShutdown` to signal that no more samples should be accepted, causing enqueue() to return false. This triggers the WAL watcher to retry with backoff. When a new shards object is created via start(), it gets a fresh softShutdown channel, so enqueuing should resume working.\n\nThe critical detail is that the WAL watcher references `t.shards` directly in its Append() call, meaning it uses whatever the current shards instance is. During a reshard operation, this reference gets updated to point to the new shards object, so the watcher should automatically start using the new queues and shutdown channel.\n\nBut if samples_pending is stuck above zero with no progress, that suggests samples are being enqueued but never actually sent. Even though Append() can write to the queue when it's not full, if the runShard goroutines never started or stopped running, the queue would fill up and subsequent Append() calls would fail, blocking the WAL watcher entirely. The old shards' goroutines would be writing to a stale `s.done` channel after `start()` creates a new one, so their completion signals won't reach the new shards' code. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_013Fg6S8eJBFpdyw6LspCzzc","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_012gBag7xV635aTVFe6AzzKU","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe intermittent stalling of remote-write shards after resharding is caused by a **race condition in the metrics counter reset** combined with **asynchronous queue shutdown timing**. When `start()` is called on new shards, it immediately resets `pendingSamples` to zero, but old shards are still in the background flushing data and decrementing this same counter. Additionally, samples enqueued during the transition window between `stop()` and `start()` may end up in queues that are being hard-shutdown before they can be sent.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1237-1266` (`start()` method) and lines 1184-1199 (`reshardLoop()`)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n\nThe resharding process has a critical flaw in how it manages the pending samples metric during queue transitions:\n\n1. **Premature Counter Reset** (line 1241):\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n       s.mtx.Lock()\n       defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- RESETS COUNTER IMMEDIATELY\n       ...\n   }\n   ```\n   This resets the counter to 0 immediately when new shards start.\n\n2. **Race with Old Shards Cleanup**:\n   ```go\n   func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n       for {\n           select {\n           case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n               t.shards.stop()         // Old shards close softShutdown, start flushing\n               t.shards.start(numShards)  // New shards created, counter reset to 0\n           ...\n           }\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n   Between `stop()` and `start()`:\n   - Old shards close `softShutdown` channel to block new enqueues\n   - Old shards begin `FlushAndShutdown()` on their queues\n   - If flush takes longer than expected, old shards hard-shutdown via context cancellation\n   - **Concurrently**: `start()` resets `pendingSamples` to 0\n   - Old shards' `runShard()` goroutines continue decrementing this counter as they finish sending\n\n3. **Hard Shutdown Timeout Behavior** (line 1286-1294):\n   ```go\n   select {\n   case <-s.done:\n       return\n   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):  // Typically 30 seconds\n   }\n   // Force an unclean shutdown\n   s.hardShutdown()  // Cancels context, old runShard goroutines exit\n   <-s.done\n   ```\n\n   If old shards don't complete flushing within `flushDeadline`:\n   - Context is cancelled via `s.hardShutdown()`\n   - Remaining samples in old queues are dropped\n   - Old `runShard` goroutines decrement `pendingSamples` for these dropped samples\n   - But counter was already reset to 0, so it never recovers\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**File: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**\n\n- **Lines 1071-1074** (`updateShardsLoop`): Updates `t.numShards` immediately after sending reshape request, before actual resharding completes\n  ```go\n  case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n      t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n      t.numShards = desiredShards  // <-- Updated before reshardLoop processes it\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1184-1199** (`reshardLoop`): Asynchronously processes reshard requests\n  ```go\n  func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n      for {\n          select {\n          case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n              t.shards.stop()         // Closes softShutdown, begins flushing\n              t.shards.start(numShards)  // Creates new queues, resets counter\n          ...\n          }\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1237-1266** (`start`): Problematic counter reset\n  ```go\n  func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n      s.mtx.Lock()\n      defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // BUG: Resets while old shards still active\n      ...\n      s.queues = newQueues\n      ...\n      for i := range n {\n          go s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1325-1327** (enqueue): Increments counter when samples enqueued\n  ```go\n  case tSample:\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n      s.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1689-1691** (updateMetrics): Decrements counter when samples sent\n  ```go\n  s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(sampleCount))\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1563-1578** (runShard hard shutdown): Drops samples when context cancelled\n  ```go\n  case <-ctx.Done():\n      droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // <-- Sub after Set(0)\n      ...\n  ```\n\n### Intermittency Explanation\n\nThe issue is intermittent because:\n\n1. **Timing-dependent**: The race condition only manifests when:\n   - Target discovery changes trigger resharding during active sample ingestion\n   - Old shards' flush takes longer than expected (> flushDeadline)\n   - New samples are enqueued during the transition window\n\n2. **Load-dependent**: Occurs more frequently under:\n   - High sample ingestion rates (more samples in flight during transition)\n   - Slow remote storage endpoints (longer flush time for old shards)\n   - Frequent target discovery changes (more resharding events)\n\n3. **Scale-dependent**: More visible at:\n   - Larger shard counts (more goroutines in transition)\n   - Higher capacity configs (more samples buffered in queues)\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**:\n   - `QueueManager` struct (manages resharding)\n   - `shards` struct (represents parallel send queues)\n   - `start()` method (initializes new shards)\n   - `stop()` method (shuts down old shards)\n   - `reshardLoop()` (processes reshard events)\n   - `updateShardsLoop()` (decides when to reshard)\n   - `enqueue()` function (enqueues samples to shards)\n   - `runShard()` goroutine (sends batches, updates metrics)\n\n2. **`storage/remote` package**:\n   - Metrics tracking pending samples\n   - WAL watcher integration that calls `Append()`\n\n## Root Cause Analysis: Why Shards Stall\n\nThe stalling occurs through this sequence:\n\n1. **Reshape triggered**: Target discovery change → desired shards change (e.g., 4 → 6)\n\n2. **Async reshard starts**:\n   ```\n   updateShardsLoop sends to reshardChan\n   reshardLoop receives: stop() old shards, start() new shards\n   ```\n\n3. **Old shards shutdown**:\n   - `stop()` closes `softShutdown` channel\n   - WAL watcher's `enqueue()` calls fail (return false)\n   - New samples in-flight retry with backoff\n\n4. **Critical race - Counter reset**:\n   - `start()` acquires write lock\n   - Sets `pendingSamples = 0` (line 1241)\n   - Creates new queues and starts new `runShard` goroutines\n   - Releases lock\n\n5. **Samples enqueued to new shards**:\n   - WAL watcher's retries succeed on new shards\n   - Samples are `Append()`ed to new queues\n   - `pendingSamples` is incremented for each sample\n\n6. **Potential stall scenarios**:\n\n   **Scenario A - Partial batch buffering**:\n   - New samples are buffered in queue's partial batch\n   - Batch doesn't fill up to capacity\n   - Batch timeout (10+ seconds) waiting for more samples\n   - If no new samples arrive, `runShard` timer eventually flushes batch\n\n   **Scenario B - Hard shutdown during transition**:\n   - Old shards exceed `flushDeadline` waiting to send\n   - `hardShutdown()` cancels old context\n   - Old `runShard` goroutines exit, dropping queued samples\n   - They call `Sub(droppedSamples)` on counter already reset to 0\n   - Counter tracking becomes inconsistent\n\n   **Scenario C - Queue channel deadlock**:\n   - Sample enqueued during transition window\n   - Ends up in old shard's batch that's never flushed\n   - Or in new shard queue that runShard never reads from\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe `start()` method should NOT reset `pendingSamples` to 0 unconditionally. Instead:\n\n1. **Preserve old shard metrics**: Don't reset the counter; let old shards naturally decrement it as they complete\n2. **Alternative**: Only reset counter AFTER confirming old shards are fully stopped\n3. **Or**: Atomically transfer pending count from old shards to new shards\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this root cause in a live system:\n\n1. **Monitor these metrics during resharding**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` (should not jump to 0)\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` (actual number of shards)\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` (target number)\n\n2. **Enable debug logging** in queue_manager:\n   - Watch for \"Remote storage resharding\" messages\n   - Check timestamps against \"Resharding done\"\n   - Look for \"(Currently resharding, skipping.)\" messages (queue blocked)\n\n3. **Examine for stuck samples**:\n   ```promql\n   # High pending with zero output rate\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending > 0\n   and\n   rate(prometheus_remote_storage_samples_total[1m]) == 0\n\n   # Check for specific shards stuck\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending\n   without (job, instance) by (shard)\n   ```\n\n4. **Look for dropped samples**:\n   - Check if `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` increased during resharding\n   - This would indicate hard shutdown occurred\n\n5. **Check logs for timeout messages**:\n   - Search for flush deadline exceeded during resharding\n   - These correlate with hard shutdown dropping samples\n\n### Prevention Measures\n\n1. **Increase `flushDeadline`** in queue config if resharding frequently fails\n2. **Reduce resharding frequency** by tuning `shardUpdateDuration` (currently 10 seconds)\n3. **Monitor resharding events** and correlation with:\n   - Target discovery changes\n   - Sample ingestion rate spikes\n   - Remote storage latency increases\n\n## Related Code\n\n- CHANGELOG.md mentions issue #7122 \"Fixed blocked resharding edge case\" (line 1457)\n- This investigation suggests the fix may have been incomplete or partially reverted\n- The core issue of counter reset during transition persists\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2348,"cache_read_input_tokens":91980,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2348},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ff4b3d24-ed86-492c-a51d-07abee1d7189","uuid":"885f413a-5043-4b53-adc9-6b5d8e15176b"}

Problematic counter reset\n  ```go\n  func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n      s.mtx.Lock()\n      defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // BUG: Resets while old shards still active\n      ...\n      s.queues = newQueues\n      ...\n      for i := range n {\n          go s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1325-1327** (enqueue): Increments counter when samples enqueued\n  ```go\n  case tSample:\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n      s.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1689-1691** (updateMetrics): Decrements counter when samples sent\n  ```go\n  s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(sampleCount))\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 1563-1578** (runShard hard shutdown): Drops samples when context cancelled\n  ```go\n  case <-ctx.Done():\n      droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n      s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // <-- Sub after Set(0)\n      ...\n  ```\n\n### Intermittency Explanation\n\nThe issue is intermittent because:\n\n1. **Timing-dependent**: The race condition only manifests when:\n   - Target discovery changes trigger resharding during active sample ingestion\n   - Old shards' flush takes longer than expected (> flushDeadline)\n   - New samples are enqueued during the transition window\n\n2. **Load-dependent**: Occurs more frequently under:\n   - High sample ingestion rates (more samples in flight during transition)\n   - Slow remote storage endpoints (longer flush time for old shards)\n   - Frequent target discovery changes (more resharding events)\n\n3. **Scale-dependent**: More visible at:\n   - Larger shard counts (more goroutines in transition)\n   - Higher capacity configs (more samples buffered in queues)\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**:\n   - `QueueManager` struct (manages resharding)\n   - `shards` struct (represents parallel send queues)\n   - `start()` method (initializes new shards)\n   - `stop()` method (shuts down old shards)\n   - `reshardLoop()` (processes reshard events)\n   - `updateShardsLoop()` (decides when to reshard)\n   - `enqueue()` function (enqueues samples to shards)\n   - `runShard()` goroutine (sends batches, updates metrics)\n\n2. **`storage/remote` package**:\n   - Metrics tracking pending samples\n   - WAL watcher integration that calls `Append()`\n\n## Root Cause Analysis: Why Shards Stall\n\nThe stalling occurs through this sequence:\n\n1. **Reshape triggered**: Target discovery change → desired shards change (e.g., 4 → 6)\n\n2. **Async reshard starts**:\n   ```\n   updateShardsLoop sends to reshardChan\n   reshardLoop receives: stop() old shards, start() new shards\n   ```\n\n3. **Old shards shutdown**:\n   - `stop()` closes `softShutdown` channel\n   - WAL watcher's `enqueue()` calls fail (return false)\n   - New samples in-flight retry with backoff\n\n4. **Critical race - Counter reset**:\n   - `start()` acquires write lock\n   - Sets `pendingSamples = 0` (line 1241)\n   - Creates new queues and starts new `runShard` goroutines\n   - Releases lock\n\n5. **Samples enqueued to new shards**:\n   - WAL watcher's retries succeed on new shards\n   - Samples are `Append()`ed to new queues\n   - `pendingSamples` is incremented for each sample\n\n6. **Potential stall scenarios**:\n\n   **Scenario A - Partial batch buffering**:\n   - New samples are buffered in queue's partial batch\n   - Batch doesn't fill up to capacity\n   - Batch timeout (10+ seconds) waiting for more samples\n   - If no new samples arrive, `runShard` timer eventually flushes batch\n\n   **Scenario B - Hard shutdown during transition**:\n   - Old shards exceed `flushDeadline` waiting to send\n   - `hardShutdown()` cancels old context\n   - Old `runShard` goroutines exit, dropping queued samples\n   - They call `Sub(droppedSamples)` on counter already reset to 0\n   - Counter tracking becomes inconsistent\n\n   **Scenario C - Queue channel deadlock**:\n   - Sample enqueued during transition window\n   - Ends up in old shard's batch that's never flushed\n   - Or in new shard queue that runShard never reads from\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe `start()` method should NOT reset `pendingSamples` to 0 unconditionally. Instead:\n\n1. **Preserve old shard metrics**: Don't reset the counter; let old shards naturally decrement it as they complete\n2. **Alternative**: Only reset counter AFTER confirming old shards are fully stopped\n3. **Or**: Atomically transfer pending count from old shards to new shards\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this root cause in a live system:\n\n1. **Monitor these metrics during resharding**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` (should not jump to 0)\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` (actual number of shards)\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` (target number)\n\n2. **Enable debug logging** in queue_manager:\n   - Watch for \"Remote storage resharding\" messages\n   - Check timestamps against \"Resharding done\"\n   - Look for \"(Currently resharding, skipping.)\" messages (queue blocked)\n\n3. **Examine for stuck samples**:\n   ```promql\n   # High pending with zero output rate\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending > 0\n   and\n   rate(prometheus_remote_storage_samples_total[1m]) == 0\n\n   # Check for specific shards stuck\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending\n   without (job, instance) by (shard)\n   ```\n\n4. **Look for dropped samples**:\n   - Check if `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` increased during resharding\n   - This would indicate hard shutdown occurred\n\n5. **Check logs for timeout messages**:\n   - Search for flush deadline exceeded during resharding\n   - These correlate with hard shutdown dropping samples\n\n### Prevention Measures\n\n1. **Increase `flushDeadline`** in queue config if resharding frequently fails\n2. **Reduce resharding frequency** by tuning `shardUpdateDuration` (currently 10 seconds)\n3. **Monitor resharding events** and correlation with:\n   - Target discovery changes\n   - Sample ingestion rate spikes\n   - Remote storage latency increases\n\n## Related Code\n\n- CHANGELOG.md mentions issue #7122 \"Fixed blocked resharding edge case\" (line 1457)\n- This investigation suggests the fix may have been incomplete or partially reverted\n- The core issue of counter reset during transition persists\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Here's a summary of what I found:\n\n## Key Findings\n\n**Root Cause:** A **race condition in the metrics counter management** during queue resharding. When new shards are started, the `pendingSamples` counter is immediately reset to 0 (via `Set(0)` at line 1241), but old shards are still running in background goroutines and decrementing this same counter. This creates a critical race condition.\n\n**The Mechanism:**\n1. Old shards begin shutting down via `stop()` which closes the `softShutdown` channel\n2. Concurrently, `start()` is called which resets `pendingSamples` to 0 while new queues are created\n3.
